## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a chemical concentration A, indicating an underlying kinetic ordinary differential equation. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are classical concentration-dependent rate laws (zero/first/second/nth order), reversible/source terms, or time-dependent effective rate constants.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate formation or depletion when another reactant is in large excess or surface-limited)
- Linear relaxation to steady state: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (net source plus first-order loss/gain; common in CSTR-like or pseudo-first-order settings)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order in A)
- First-order approach to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (formation with constant source balanced by first-order removal; yields exponential approach to A = c0/c1)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction where both reactants track A or A represents one of two equal reactants)
- Nth-order (power-law) rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global rate order or complex mechanism lumped into an effective order)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating production with depletion/limitation, e.g., autocatalysis with finite resource)
- Reversible first-order (A â†” products) with equilibrium shift: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (forward first-order loss opposed by backward term proportional to product pool)
- Time-dependent pseudo-first-order (exponentially changing activity): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant varies exponentially in time due to catalyst activation/deactivation or changing environment)
- Time-dependent pseudo-first-order (linear drift): dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * t) * A (rate constant drifts approximately linearly over the observation window)
- Mixed-order (parallel pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular and bimolecular consumption routes)
- Self-inhibition / finite-capacity effect (nonlinear damping): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (effective rate slows at high A due to crowding/transport limits; rational saturation-like loss)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (dA_dt âˆ‌ -A), it indicates first-order/pseudo-first-order kinetics with an exponential decay in A over t.
- If dA_dt scales like -A**2 or -A**n, it suggests bimolecular or higher-order/global-order kinetics; depletion accelerates strongly with concentration.
- A constant term in dA_dt (additive c0) implies zero-order production/consumption (surface-limited, constant feed, or another reactant held constant).
- A form dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A indicates relaxation toward a steady-state concentration A* = c0/c1 (balance of constant source and first-order sink).
- Presence of both linear and quadratic terms (e.g., -A - A**2) indicates parallel reaction pathways or competing mechanisms with different molecularities.
- A factor like (c1 - A) multiplying A (A*(c1-A)) implies self-enhancement with eventual limitation (autocatalysis with depletion/carrying-capacity behavior).
- Explicit time dependence in the rate prefactor (e.g., exp(c*t), (c0+c1*t)) indicates changing effective rate constants due to catalyst deactivation/activation, temperature ramps, or evolving medium properties.
- Rational dependence on A (e.g., A/(A+c1) or 1/(A+c1)) suggests inhibition, finite-capacity/transport limitations, or mechanistic quasi-steady reductions that create nonlinear damping.
